## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material. Stress depends on strain through constitutive laws (linear or nonlinear), while temperature modifies elastic moduli, yield strength, and hardening behavior through thermal softening or thermally activated mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity with constant modulus)
- Temperature-dependent linear elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (modulus linearly decreasing with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (quadratic): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (polynomial temperature dependence of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Ramberg-Osgood type nonlinear stress-strain)
- Temperature-dependent power-law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated power-law behavior)
- Johnson-Cook type model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Ludwik-Hollomon with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (c2 - T)**c3 (power-law hardening with melting-type softening)
- Voce hardening (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (c2 + c3 * T) (saturating hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Arrhenius-type thermal activation: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * (1/T)) (thermally activated deformation)
- Polynomial constitutive law: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic with higher-order terms)
- Bilinear thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 - c1 * T) (linear strain with linear thermal softening factor)
- Hyperbolic sine creep law: sigma = c0 * sinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (hyperbolic sine flow rule)
- Neo-Hookean type with temperature: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * epsilon**3) (hyperelastic-like with thermal dependence)
- Swift hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * exp(c3 * T) (offset power-law with thermal factor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of elastic modulus → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T) or (c0 + c1*T) multiplying the strain-dependent term
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating asymptotic stress at large strains
- Thermally activated processes → exp(c/T) or exp(-c*T) multiplicative factors reflecting Arrhenius-type mechanisms
- Nonlinear elasticity in large deformation → odd-power polynomial in epsilon (epsilon, epsilon**3, epsilon**5) to preserve symmetry
- Melting/critical temperature effects → (T_m - T)**c form where stress vanishes at a critical temperature
- Strain-rate and temperature equivalence → in many materials, increasing T is equivalent to decreasing strain rate, suggesting log(T) or 1/T coupling
- Elastic-plastic transition → piecewise or smooth transition combining linear (c*epsilon) at small strains with power-law (epsilon**n) at large strains
- Multiplicative decomposition of strain and temperature effects → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), suggesting separable functional forms as a first approximation
